## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables (sigma: stress, epsilon: strain, T: temperature) indicate a constitutive law identification problem for a solid, where stress depends on mechanical deformation and temperature via elastic modulus changes, thermal expansion, and temperature-dependent hardening/softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (1D linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (thermoelastic stiffness variation)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (quadratic-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (curved E(T) dependence over wider T range)
- Thermal expansion / constrained thermoelasticity: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mismatch between mechanical strain and free thermal strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (moderate nonlinearity in elastic response)
- Cubic elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (large-strain elastic nonlinearity fit form)
- Power-law strain hardening (Hollomon/Ludwik-type): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (plastic flow with work hardening)
- Logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * log(1 + c2 * epsilon) (hardening with diminishing slope at larger strain)
- Voce-type saturating hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (flow stress approaches an asymptote with strain)
- Thermal softening factor (rational): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) / (1 + c3 * T) (strength decreases with temperature, avoids negative stresses)
- Thermo-hardening/softening cross-term expansion: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (first-order coupling between deformation and temperature)
- Eyring-style smooth nonlinearity (activation-like shape): sigma = c0 + c1 * asinh(c2 * epsilon) + c3 * T (captures rapid initial rise then slower increase with strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Purely elastic response at small strain often implies sigma proportional to epsilon; deviations suggest nonlinear elasticity or early plasticity.
- Thermal expansion under constraint produces an effective shift in strain: sigma tends to depend on (epsilon - c * (T - T0)), yielding near-zero stress along a “free expansion” line.
- Elastic modulus typically decreases with temperature in many solids, so an E(T)*epsilon structure with E(T) decreasing in T is common.
- Yield/flow stress commonly softens with temperature; multiplicative factors like 1/(1 + c*T) help enforce monotone weakening without sign flips.
- Plastic work hardening is often concave in epsilon; power-law (epsilon**n) and log(1+c*epsilon) capture decreasing tangent modulus with strain.
- Many metals exhibit saturation of hardening at large strain; asymptotic forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) represent approach to a limiting flow stress.
- Cross-terms epsilon*T can represent thermo-mechanical coupling where temperature changes the slope of the stress–strain curve rather than only adding an offset.
- If data show curvature that changes with T, prefer factored forms like (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2)*epsilon over additive sigma = f(epsilon) + g(T), reflecting modulus control.

1. `epsilon^c1 * exp(c2/T)` — a power of epsilon times Arrhenius-like term

**For `Abs(epsilon)^c` with epsilon ≥ 0:** This equals `epsilon^c`, which matches.

**For `Max(0, epsilon)^c` with epsilon ≥ 0:** This equals `epsilon^c`, which matches.

- `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)` (not `exp(c*T)` or `exp(c*epsilon)`)
